<gmapID>0x54d1557ac90dde75:0x40c58f54ee05b963<//gmapID>< pictures>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNR5yl_ytd5T1H6T06YHWM4O_-1AbbMSvjLgHun=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pictures>

< UserId.>
109958693559147293422<//UserId.>
< username>
Jessica Heiden<//username>
<date>1520875417781</date><Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
There are a lot of fun, cheap, easy crafts you can try, and they provide all the materials! I had fun painting rocks and enjoying a cider drink. Prices are fair; you can paint 1 rock for $2.

We're going back to try string art--be aware, they said the large size can take 3 hours! A few friends are going back for the wine bottle etching class. We were going to join, but will be out of state.

The layout is okay. The front has the bar and seating, including comfy chairs and sofas. There is an awesome giant mural on the wall. Then there's a narrow hallway with staff offices and past that it opens up to the large crafting room. It would be nice if these areas could be a little more integrated (I think that narrow hallway acts too much as a divider). I spent my time going between my friends in the front and friends in the back, but once I started crafting I stayed in that room, so then we were separated. I worry that people might come in the 'front' entrance (I think there's also an entrance from the Plaza to the crafts side) and get stuck at the bar area without venturing back to the crafts area, which would really be a shame. Maybe showcasing more of the crafts (including pricing and instructions) in the bar area would intrigue people to walk back. Also, making sure the bartenders know about the crafts would help since they are talking to the customers when they order. Maybe cross-training would help integrate the arts with the drafts.

Really relaxed vibe. A few hipsters, but overall it felt more laid back than 'ahh is this place too trendy for me?'. It's really cool that the owner's mom is visiting from the Midwest to help out her daughter. We were there on International Women's Day and she helped cheer on the girl power vibe.<//Review>

First, I will definitely give the coffee, any kind, a 5-star. Location, 5 star, for UCSD, Bethel Seminary and a couple of churches nearby for a Sunday after church drink. < review>
Loved this place. So peaceful and beautiful. The rooms were nice, clean, and had personality to it. We loved the (electric) fireplace in our room. They have a Nespresso maker in the room (complimentary) so we were able to drink coffee while chatting by the fireplace. They also give a complimentary half bottle of wine. It wasn't the best wine I've ever had, but hey, it's free! Room service was fast and the food tasted great! The pool is on the smaller side, but still really nice with great views (when standing). They also have free sunscreen. There are only 92 rooms/suites here, so the place feels quiet. They also gave a Town car that will take you within 5 miles of the resort so we were able to utilize it when we went out for dinner. Their main dining room has great views and awesome service. (The food was good too). Definitely recommend this place and can't wait to go back.< /review>

<review>For a hotel that has rooms for $600 a night (Valentines day 2020 weekend), I was definitely expecting a better experience at their restaurant. My Husband and I were celebrating my birthday and valentines day this weekend. He wanted to take me to some really great restaurants in the area, and this was supposed to be one of them. For the price and the quality of not only the food but the staff as well... you can for sure skip this place.
Our reservation was at 7:15 pm last night. We were seated at a really great table by the ledge of the deck overlooking Santa Barbara. The restaurant was fairly quiet and most people left due to finishing dinner so our experience was somewhat private. The view was spectacular, but that's where the spectacularness ended.
We were greeted by an older woman who was going to be our server for the night. We had brought our own bottle of wine ($45 corkage which was absolutely fine) due to us visiting multiple wineries in the area over the weekend. She asked what water we wanted and we asked her to open our wine. She took 20 mins to come open our wine (which was unfortunate because I wanted it to breathe a little before our enjoyment) and was pretty snobbish about us bringing our wine anyway. Let me add, the wine list here is not impressive. They are selling $20 wines for 5x+... like selling duck horn for $230- are you guys nuts?
We moved onto ordering our food. We ordered: The Yellowfin Tuna Tartare, Heirloom Tomato Salad, Diver Scallops and Hope Ranch Mussels. My husband and I often split dinners, and do a lot of family style sharing. The waitress didn't seem too thrilled about that.
The Yellowfin Tuna with soy truffle vinaigrette, lime, daikon, taroroot: Was really great. Its a super small portion compared to others I've had, but it was very fresh and I thought the flavors were great.
Heirloom Tomato Salad with scallions, olives, feta, piquillo peppers, lemon, California olive oil, fresh herbs: Not so much. In the photo you will actually see how unripe the salad was. We could hardly cut into it, it didn't taste great but it also didn't look great. We sent it back, the chef sent his apologies and the waitress could only talk about how this chef was French and was sooooo great. Well it doesn't take a really great chef to understand that the Tomatoes weren't ripe, and that he should not have sent that out.
Instead we got the Little Gem Lettuce with walnut vinaigrette, ricotta salata, tomatoes, radishes, herbs. I was actually expecting the Gem lettuce to be smaller, this was like a full on heart of romaine. There wasn't enough salad dressing on it, and the chef didn't even core the romaine heart. It was like gem lettuce on steroids and without any flavor.
Diver Scallops with squid ink fried rice, bok choy, sea asparagus, kingcrabfritter, yuzu-ginger reduction:
The scallops were cooked perfectly, surprisingly. You could actually cut it with your fork (which often times places overcook these delicate scallops) and they were nice and buttery. The flavoring was ok, nothing to really rave about but they were good. The squid ink fried rice was the one thing we were really excited about because we love squid ink. Sadly it did not have much flavor and left us a little disappointed.
Hope Ranch Mussels with grilled octopus, fennel seeds, preservedlemon, herbs:
Sadly another dish we were not so impressed with. The mussels were tough, and overcooked. The reason I know they were over cooked is because they fell out of their shells and as we pulled out shells expecting Mussels in them, we had to dig to the bottom of the dish. The grilled octopus was also tough, normally this is served tender as well. The flavor of the dish was pretty good, but the fact that it was over done was disappointing. We ended up putting the squid ink rice in the sauce of this dish to make our experience a little better.
The truffle fries included like 0 parm, we got a side of parm chunks lol.
Besides the food, our dining experience was awful.< /review><rating>1< /rating><name>Jennifer K<//name><userid>111232672016929890675< /userid></record></dataset><record>

<text>El Encanto sits on an absolutely perfect piece of land high up in the hills of Santa Barbara. The entrance is subdued and discreet, which makes your visit feel that much more special, despite being just a short ride away from town. You can easily spend a day or two relaxing by the pool and just enjoying all the hotel has to offer, but if you're so inclined, the surrounding area has plenty to offer as well: beach, golf, vineyards, etc.

Belmond's portfolio is quite interesting. They have properties all over the world, operate luxury train services in several countries, own the legendary 21 Club in New York City ‚Äî needless to say they've got a lot going on. They've managed to establish a fairly coherent brand in the luxury space and it feels like they'll keep getting better and better. The draw here is without a doubt the property though. The rooms are beautiful, the pool is picturesque, and cocktails outside with views of the ocean are ideal.

The restaurant isn't memorable and the fitness area could use more attention - why every luxury hotel doesn't have a Peleton will never cease to confuse me, but overall El Encanto delivers high scores across the board.</text><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPkEjcDEmI0AjDsarWPXPSzlT0RoJDjotravNru=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNxYR35X4frcFUNqoQbVfM-XzdlUK-T7Zqljj9M=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNCfIjVEYFy12QqVb4G2CiigTTdHeulMhBiMaQz=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pictures>< response>

<Review>This is a lovely, quiet, beautiful, restful hotel. The website doesnt do it justice. Perched inland and up in the hills of Santa Barbara, the hotel has a free shuttle that will take you anywhere within a 5 mile radius - which means all of downtown SB, beaches, parks, the Mission and other sites. The efficient and welcoming staff hums around the campus and is present immediately when needed. The pool is lovely; the workout room is reasonably useful and the grounds and gardens are fabulous. But, the best feature is the terrace off the dining room where everyone wants to eat; guests and locals alike. The breakfast fruit and eggs bene were among the best weve ever had. It was chilly in the mornings this past June and the staff had the heaters cranking and the blankets handy which was a real treat since we really wanted to be outside. We found the salt encrusted meats at dinner time a bit too salty. The rooms were spacious and the staff very accommodating. Its easy to see why El Encanto gets rated so highly - I wasnt fully convinced until we stayed. Well go back for sure.< /Review><Pics>None< /Pics>< resp>
None< /resp>

The location is high in the hills of Santa Barbara lending to breathtaking views over downtown. Bungalows scattered about the grounds house luxurious rooms with too level amenities. An absolute five-star experience!<//review>

<Rate>4</Rate><review>This is an updated review (original post was in November 2018.)  There was a change in management which resulted in a follow up phone call and an offer to stay on site for a weekend.  We were happy to accept the offer and had a very nice stay.  The bungalow was great: clean and well appointed.  They made several nice gestures like having food and wine in the room as well as covering the cost of valet. Nearly everyone we interacted with was lovely and warm.  I've worked in hospitality, of course I know it's their job to treat us well, but even one weird conversation can really make or break a guest's experience.  Leading into our second night we received a phone call asking when we'd be leaving the room.  Panicked, I explained what was in my email confirmation and the staff member (sounding very annoyed) said "Oooookay.  I guess we'll extend your stay?"  I felt terrible -- had I misunderstood the arrangement? Was someone else's stay messed up because we hadn't left the room?  I contacted the general manager who sorted it out immediately and we received a follow up apology (awkward, but appreciated.) We greatly appreciated the opportunity to have a better experience with the hotel.  My advice: whether you're planning a stay or an event, double check everything and put it all in writing.</review>< pics>

Our stay at the Belmond was simply majestic. From the moment you pull up, you're treated like royalty. The resort is flawless, beautiful in every way. The staff is cheerful, warm and inviting at all times. The views of Santa Barbara cannot be beat. Again, our stay at the Belmond was flawless. If you want to experience royal service, unmatched views and an all around incredible stay, there is no better in SB than the Belmond.</text>
